â”‚ â”‚ +## [2.0.2] - 2023-04-06
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +### Added
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +- Beta support for [optimizer reinitialization](https://finetuning-scheduler.readthedocs.io/en/stable/advanced/optimizer_reinitialization.html). Resolves [#6](https://github.com/speediedan/finetuning-scheduler/issues/6)
â”‚ â”‚ +- Use structural typing for Fine-Tuning Scheduler supported optimizers with ``ParamGroupAddable``
â”‚ â”‚ +- Support for ``jsonargparse`` version ``4.20.1``
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +### Changed
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +- During schedule phase transitions, the latest LR state will be restored before proceeding with the next phase configuration and execution (mostly relevant to lr scheduler and optimizer reinitialization but also improves configuration when restoring best checkpoints across multiple depths)
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +### Fixed
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +- Allow sharded optimizers ``ZeroRedundancyOptimizer`` to be properly reconfigured if necessary in the context of ``enforce_phase0_params`` set to ``True``.
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚

â”‚ â”‚  
â”‚ â”‚  [FinetuningScheduler](https://finetuning-scheduler.readthedocs.io/en/stable/api/finetuning_scheduler.fts.html#finetuning_scheduler.fts.FinetuningScheduler) is simple to use yet powerful, offering a number of features that facilitate model research and exploration:
â”‚ â”‚  
â”‚ â”‚  - easy specification of flexible fine-tuning schedules with explicit or regex-based parameter selection
â”‚ â”‚    - implicit schedules for initial/naive model exploration
â”‚ â”‚    - explicit schedules for performance tuning, fine-grained behavioral experimentation and computational efficiency
â”‚ â”‚  - automatic restoration of best per-phase checkpoints driven by iterative application of early-stopping criteria to each fine-tuning phase

â”‚ â”‚  ______________________________________________________________________
â”‚ â”‚  
â”‚ â”‚  ## Continuous Integration
â”‚ â”‚  
â”‚ â”‚  Fine-Tuning Scheduler is rigorously tested across multiple CPUs, GPUs and against major Python and PyTorch versions. Each Fine-Tuning Scheduler minor release (major.minor.patch) is paired with a Lightning minor release (e.g. Fine-Tuning Scheduler 2.0 depends upon Lightning 2.0).
â”‚ â”‚  
â”‚ â”‚  To ensure maximum stability, the latest Lightning patch release fully tested with Fine-Tuning Scheduler is set as a maximum dependency in Fine-Tuning Scheduler's requirements.txt (e.g. \<= 1.7.1). If you'd like to test a specific Lightning patch version greater than that currently in Fine-Tuning Scheduler's requirements.txt, it will likely work but you should install Fine-Tuning Scheduler from source and update the requirements.txt as desired.
â”‚ â”‚

â”‚ â”‚ â”‚  Continuous Integration Fine-Tuning Scheduler is rigorously tested across
â”‚ â”‚ â”‚  multiple CPUs, GPUs and against major Python and PyTorch versions. Each Fine-
â”‚ â”‚ â”‚  Tuning Scheduler minor release (major.minor.patch) is paired with a Lightning
â”‚ â”‚ â”‚  minor release (e.g. Fine-Tuning Scheduler 2.0 depends upon Lightning 2.0). To
â”‚ â”‚ â”‚  ensure maximum stability, the latest Lightning patch release fully tested with
â”‚ â”‚ â”‚  Fine-Tuning Scheduler is set as a maximum dependency in Fine-Tuning Scheduler's

â”‚ â”‚ +    def _add_pgs_config_lrs(
â”‚ â”‚ +        self,
â”‚ â”‚ +        optimizer: ParamGroupAddable,
â”‚ â”‚ +        next_tl: Dict,

â”‚ â”‚ +        is_target_depth: bool,

â”‚ â”‚ +    ) -> None:
â”‚ â”‚ +        """Add optimizer parameter groups and potentially reinitialize/reconfigure the learning rate scheduler
â”‚ â”‚ +        according to a given schedule phase configuration.
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +        Args:
â”‚ â”‚ +            optimizer (:class:`~finetuning_scheduler.types.ParamGroupAddable`): The supported optimizer instance to
â”‚ â”‚ +                which parameter groups will be configured and added.
â”‚ â”‚ +            next_tl (Dict): A dictionary containing the schedule configuration associated with the current phase
â”‚ â”‚ +                context.
â”‚ â”‚ +            depth (int): The current target depth.
â”‚ â”‚ +            is_target_depth (bool): Whether this restoration stage is the current target depth.
â”‚ â”‚ +            pre_reinit_state (Tuple): Contingent on restoration context, lr scheduler and optimizer lr state to restore.
â”‚ â”‚ +        """
â”‚ â”‚ +        # if the target depth is 0, lr scheduler reinitialization should not be executed
â”‚ â”‚ +        new_scheduler_cfg = (self.reinit_lr_cfg or next_tl.get("new_lr_scheduler", None)) if depth > 0 else None
â”‚ â”‚ +        if is_target_depth and depth > 0:
â”‚ â”‚ +            # NB: The latest optimizer and lr scheduler lr state will be re-applied to all existing param groups before
â”‚ â”‚ +            # implementing the next phase.

â”‚ â”‚ +            no_decay=getattr(self.pl_module, "no_decay", None),
â”‚ â”‚ +            apply_lambdas=self.apply_lambdas_new_pgs,
â”‚ â”‚ +        )
â”‚ â”‚ +        if new_scheduler_cfg:
â”‚ â”‚ +            self.reinit_lr_scheduler(
â”‚ â”‚ +                new_lr_scheduler=new_scheduler_cfg, trainer=self.pl_module.trainer, optimizer=optimizer
â”‚ â”‚ +            )
â”‚ â”‚ +        else:
â”‚ â”‚ +            self._maybe_warn_lr_lambdas()

â”‚ â”‚ -<img width="300px" src="https://github.com/speediedan/finetuning-scheduler/raw/v2.0.1/docs/source/_static/images/fts/fts_explicit_loss_anim.gif" alt="FinetuningScheduler explicit loss animation" align="right"/>

â”‚ â”‚  
â”‚ â”‚  [FinetuningScheduler](https://finetuning-scheduler.readthedocs.io/en/stable/api/finetuning_scheduler.fts.html#finetuning_scheduler.fts.FinetuningScheduler) is simple to use yet powerful, offering a number of features that facilitate model research and exploration:
â”‚ â”‚  
â”‚ â”‚  - easy specification of flexible fine-tuning schedules with explicit or regex-based parameter selection
â”‚ â”‚    - implicit schedules for initial/naive model exploration
â”‚ â”‚    - explicit schedules for performance tuning, fine-grained behavioral experimentation and computational efficiency
â”‚ â”‚  - automatic restoration of best per-phase checkpoints driven by iterative application of early-stopping criteria to each fine-tuning phase

â”‚ â”‚  ______________________________________________________________________
â”‚ â”‚  
â”‚ â”‚  ## Continuous Integration
â”‚ â”‚  
â”‚ â”‚  Fine-Tuning Scheduler is rigorously tested across multiple CPUs, GPUs and against major Python and PyTorch versions. Each Fine-Tuning Scheduler minor release (major.minor.patch) is paired with a Lightning minor release (e.g. Fine-Tuning Scheduler 2.0 depends upon Lightning 2.0).
â”‚ â”‚  
â”‚ â”‚  To ensure maximum stability, the latest Lightning patch release fully tested with Fine-Tuning Scheduler is set as a maximum dependency in Fine-Tuning Scheduler's requirements.txt (e.g. \<= 1.7.1). If you'd like to test a specific Lightning patch version greater than that currently in Fine-Tuning Scheduler's requirements.txt, it will likely work but you should install Fine-Tuning Scheduler from source and update the requirements.txt as desired.
â”‚ â”‚

â”‚ â”‚ â”‚  multiple CPUs, GPUs and against major Python and PyTorch versions. Each Fine-
â”‚ â”‚ â”‚  Tuning Scheduler minor release (major.minor.patch) is paired with a Lightning
â”‚ â”‚ â”‚  minor release (e.g. Fine-Tuning Scheduler 2.0 depends upon Lightning 2.0). To
â”‚ â”‚ â”‚  ensure maximum stability, the latest Lightning patch release fully tested with
â”‚ â”‚ â”‚  Fine-Tuning Scheduler is set as a maximum dependency in Fine-Tuning Scheduler's

â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +@pytest.mark.parametrize(
â”‚ â”‚ +    "explicit_mode, reinit_optim_only, use_curr_optim_pg",
â”‚ â”‚ +    [
â”‚ â”‚ +        pytest.param(True, True, False, id="explicit_optim"),
â”‚ â”‚ +        pytest.param(True, False, False, id="explicit_optimlr"),
â”‚ â”‚ +        pytest.param(False, True, False, id="implicit_optim"),
â”‚ â”‚ +        pytest.param(False, False, False, id="implicit_optimlr"),
â”‚ â”‚ +        pytest.param(True, False, True, id="explicit_optimlr_use_curr"),
â”‚ â”‚ +        pytest.param(False, False, True, id="implicit_optimlr_use_curr"),
â”‚ â”‚ +    ],
â”‚ â”‚ +)
â”‚ â”‚ +def test_finetuningscheduling_reinit_optim(
â”‚ â”‚ +    tmpdir, boring_ft_schedule, explicit_mode: bool, reinit_optim_only: bool, use_curr_optim_pg: bool
â”‚ â”‚ +):
â”‚ â”‚ +    """Inspect optimizer state within the training process to ensure it is taking the expected path in both
â”‚ â”‚ +    explicit and implict fine-tuning modes."""
â”‚ â”‚ +    seed_everything(42)
â”‚ â”‚ +    reinit_optim_cfg, reinit_lr_cfg = None, None
â”‚ â”‚ +    if explicit_mode:
â”‚ â”‚ +        if reinit_optim_only:
â”‚ â”‚ +            ft_schedule = boring_ft_schedule[6]
â”‚ â”‚ +        else:
â”‚ â”‚ +            ft_schedule = boring_ft_schedule[10] if use_curr_optim_pg else boring_ft_schedule[7]
â”‚ â”‚ +    else:  # implicit mode tests
â”‚ â”‚ +        reinit_optim_cfg = IMP_REINIT_OPTIM_CFG
â”‚ â”‚ +        if not reinit_optim_only:
â”‚ â”‚ +            reinit_lr_cfg = IMP_REINIT_LR_OPTIM_USE_CURR_CFG if use_curr_optim_pg else IMP_REINIT_LR_OPTIM_CFG
â”‚ â”‚ +        ft_schedule = None
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +    model = FinetuningSchedulerBoringModel(diverge_on_epoch=1)
â”‚ â”‚ +    callbacks = [
â”‚ â”‚ +        OptInspectFTS(
â”‚ â”‚ +            expected_state=EXPECTED_REINIT_OPTIM_STATE[(explicit_mode, reinit_optim_only, use_curr_optim_pg)],
â”‚ â”‚ +            lrs_state=EXPECTED_REINIT_OPTIM_LR_STATE[(explicit_mode, reinit_optim_only, use_curr_optim_pg)],
â”‚ â”‚ +            reinit_optim_cfg=reinit_optim_cfg,
â”‚ â”‚ +            reinit_lr_cfg=reinit_lr_cfg,
â”‚ â”‚ +            ft_schedule=ft_schedule,
â”‚ â”‚ +            logging_level=DEBUG,
â”‚ â”‚ +            # state_log_dir=tmpdir,
â”‚ â”‚ +        ),
â”‚ â”‚ +        FTSEarlyStopping(monitor="val_loss", patience=2),
â”‚ â”‚ +    ]
â”‚ â”‚ +    trainer = Trainer(default_root_dir=tmpdir, callbacks=callbacks, devices=1)
â”‚ â”‚ +    trainer.fit(model)
â”‚ â”‚ +    finetuningscheduler_callback = get_fts(trainer)
â”‚ â”‚ +    assert finetuningscheduler_callback.depth_remaining == 0
â”‚ â”‚ +    assert finetuningscheduler_callback.curr_depth == 3
â”‚ â”‚ +    assert finetuningscheduler_callback.curr_depth == finetuningscheduler_callback.max_depth
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +EXPECTED_REINIT_OPTIM_LR_NODECAY_STATE = {
â”‚ â”‚ +    **COMMON_LR_INIT_PATH,
â”‚ â”‚ +    4: (0.00021, 0.00021, 1e-05, 1e-05),
â”‚ â”‚ +    5: (0.000147, 0.000147, 7e-06, 7e-06),
â”‚ â”‚ +    6: (0.002, 0.002, 1e-05, 1e-05, 3e-06, 3e-06),
â”‚ â”‚ +    7: (0.0004, 0.0004, 2e-06, 2e-06, 6e-07, 6e-07),
â”‚ â”‚ +    8: (8e-05, 8e-05, 4e-07, 4e-07, 1.2e-07, 1e-05, 1e-05),
â”‚ â”‚ +    9: (1.6e-05, 1.6e-05, 8e-08, 8e-08, 2.4e-08, 2e-06, 2e-06),
â”‚ â”‚ +}
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +EXPECTED_REINIT_OPTIM_NODECAY_STATE = {
â”‚ â”‚ +    **COMMON_OPTIM_INIT_PATH,
â”‚ â”‚ +    4: (1, 2, 4, 0, 0, 1, 4, 4, 0, 0, 4, (1, 1, 1, 1), "Adam", 256, 0.00021),
â”‚ â”‚ +    5: (1, 2, 5, 0, 0, 1, 4, 4, 0, 0, 4, (1, 1, 1, 1), "Adam", 320, 0.00021),
â”‚ â”‚ +    6: (2, 1, 6, 0, 0, 1, 6, 6, 0, 0, 6, (1, 1, 1, 1, 1, 1), "SGD", 384, 0.002),
â”‚ â”‚ +    7: (2, 1, 7, 0, 0, 1, 6, 6, 0, 0, 6, (1, 1, 1, 1, 1, 1), "SGD", 448, 0.002),
â”‚ â”‚ +    8: (3, 0, 8, 0, 0, 1, 8, 7, 0, 0, 7, (2, 1, 1, 1, 1, 1, 1), "SGD", 512, 0.002),
â”‚ â”‚ +    9: (3, 0, 9, 0, 0, 1, 8, 7, 0, 0, 7, (2, 1, 1, 1, 1, 1, 1), "SGD", 576, 0.002),

â”‚ â”‚ +def test_finetuningscheduling_reinit_optimlr_nodecay(tmpdir, boring_ft_schedule):
â”‚ â”‚ +    """Inspect optimizer state within the training process to ensure it is taking the expected path in both
â”‚ â”‚ +    explicit and implict fine-tuning modes."""
â”‚ â”‚ +    seed_everything(42)
â”‚ â”‚ +    no_decay = ["bias"]
â”‚ â”‚ +    ft_schedule = boring_ft_schedule[7]
â”‚ â”‚ +    model = FinetuningSchedulerBoringModel(diverge_on_epoch=1, no_decay=no_decay)
â”‚ â”‚ +    callbacks = [
â”‚ â”‚ +        OptInspectFTS(
â”‚ â”‚ +            expected_state=EXPECTED_REINIT_OPTIM_NODECAY_STATE,
â”‚ â”‚ +            lrs_state=EXPECTED_REINIT_OPTIM_LR_NODECAY_STATE,
â”‚ â”‚ +            ft_schedule=ft_schedule,
â”‚ â”‚ +            logging_level=DEBUG,
â”‚ â”‚ +            # state_log_dir=tmpdir,
â”‚ â”‚ +        ),
â”‚ â”‚ +        FTSEarlyStopping(monitor="val_loss", patience=2),
â”‚ â”‚ +    ]
â”‚ â”‚ +    trainer = Trainer(default_root_dir=tmpdir, callbacks=callbacks, devices=1)
â”‚ â”‚ +    trainer.fit(model)
â”‚ â”‚ +    finetuningscheduler_callback = get_fts(trainer)
â”‚ â”‚ +    assert finetuningscheduler_callback.depth_remaining == 0
â”‚ â”‚ +    assert finetuningscheduler_callback.curr_depth == 3

â”‚ â”‚ +        5: (1, 2, 5, 0, 0, 1, 4, 2, 0, 0, 2, (2, 2), "Adam", 320, 0.00021),

â”‚ â”‚ +        **COMMON_LR_INIT_PATH,
â”‚ â”‚ +        4: (0.0, 0.0),  # our lambdalr at step 0, base_lr set via optim `initial_lr`=0.00021 (for pg 0, 1e-05 for pg 1)
â”‚ â”‚ +        5: (0.0001344, 6.4e-06),  # after 64 steps out of 100 warmup, 0.64 the way to 0.00021 (for pg 0)
â”‚ â”‚ +        6: (0.000203467, 9.689e-06, 3e-06),  # after 128 steps, lambda lr returns 0.9688... of the base 0.00021
â”‚ â”‚ +        7: (0.000188533, 8.978e-06, 2.693e-06),  # after 192 steps, lambda lr returns 0.8977... of the base 0.00021
â”‚ â”‚ +        8: (0.0001736, 8.267e-06, 2.48e-06, 1e-05),  # after 256 steps proper lambda lr
â”‚ â”‚ +        9: (0.000158667, 7.556e-06, 2.267e-06, 7.556e-06),  # after 320 steps proper lambda lr
â”‚ â”‚ +    },
â”‚ â”‚ +    "reinit_optim_only_rlrop": {
â”‚ â”‚ +        **COMMON_LR_INIT_PATH,
â”‚ â”‚ +        4: (1.5e-06, 1e-05),
â”‚ â”‚ +        5: (1.5e-06, 1e-05),
â”‚ â”‚ +        6: (1.5e-06, 1e-05, 3e-06),
â”‚ â”‚ +        7: (2e-07, 1e-06, 3e-07),  # did not improve so lr reduced
â”‚ â”‚ +        8: (2e-07, 1e-06, 3e-07, 1e-05),
â”‚ â”‚ +        9: (2e-07, 1e-06, 3e-07, 1e-05),  # DID improve from best so lr is not reduced
â”‚ â”‚ +    },
â”‚ â”‚ +}
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +@pytest.mark.parametrize(
â”‚ â”‚ +    "reinit_optim_lr_key, ft_sched_idx",
â”‚ â”‚ +    [
â”‚ â”‚ +        ("reinit_optim_only_lambdalr", 8),
â”‚ â”‚ +        ("reinit_optim_only_rlrop", 9),
â”‚ â”‚ +    ],
â”‚ â”‚ +    ids=["reinit_optim_only_lambdalr", "reinit_optim_only_rlrop"],
â”‚ â”‚ +)
â”‚ â”‚ +def test_finetuningscheduling_reinit_optim_special_lr(tmpdir, boring_ft_schedule, reinit_optim_lr_key, ft_sched_idx):
â”‚ â”‚ +    """Inspect optimizer state within the training process to ensure it is taking the expected path in both
â”‚ â”‚ +    explicit and implict fine-tuning modes."""
â”‚ â”‚ +    seed_everything(42)
â”‚ â”‚ +    ft_schedule = boring_ft_schedule[ft_sched_idx]
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +    model = FinetuningSchedulerBoringModel(diverge_on_epoch=1)
â”‚ â”‚ +    callbacks = [
â”‚ â”‚ +        OptInspectFTS(
â”‚ â”‚ +            expected_state=EXPECTED_REINIT_OPTIM_SPEC_STATE[reinit_optim_lr_key],
â”‚ â”‚ +            lrs_state=EXPECTED_REINIT_OPTIM_LR_SPEC_STATE[reinit_optim_lr_key],
â”‚ â”‚ +            ft_schedule=ft_schedule,
â”‚ â”‚ +            logging_level=DEBUG,
â”‚ â”‚ +            # state_log_dir=tmpdir,
â”‚ â”‚ +        ),
â”‚ â”‚ +        FTSEarlyStopping(monitor="val_loss", patience=2),
â”‚ â”‚ +    ]
â”‚ â”‚ +    trainer = Trainer(default_root_dir=tmpdir, callbacks=callbacks, devices=1)
â”‚ â”‚ +    trainer.fit(model)
â”‚ â”‚ +    finetuningscheduler_callback = get_fts(trainer)
â”‚ â”‚ +    assert finetuningscheduler_callback.depth_remaining == 0
â”‚ â”‚ +    assert finetuningscheduler_callback.curr_depth == 3
â”‚ â”‚ +    assert finetuningscheduler_callback.curr_depth == finetuningscheduler_callback.max_depth
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚ +
â”‚ â”‚  IMP_REINIT_LR_CFG = {
â”‚ â”‚      "lr_scheduler_init": {
â”‚ â”‚          "class_path": "torch.optim.lr_scheduler.StepLR",
â”‚ â”‚          "init_args": {"step_size": 1, "gamma": 0.7, "verbose": True},
â”‚ â”‚      },
â”‚ â”‚      "pl_lrs_cfg": {"interval": "epoch", "frequency": 1, "name": "Custom_Reinit_LR"},
â”‚ â”‚  }
â”‚ â”‚  
â”‚ â”‚  
â”‚ â”‚  EXPECTED_LR_STATE = {
â”‚ â”‚ -    (False, False): {
â”‚ â”‚ -        "max_depth": 3,
â”‚ â”‚ -        0: (0.001,),
â”‚ â”‚ -        1: (0.0007,),
â”‚ â”‚ -        2: (0.00049,),
â”‚ â”‚ -        3: (0.000343,),
â”‚ â”‚ -        4: (0.0002401,),
